NO APPEAL FROM
THE COLLECTOR
Ruling in Transit Cases
Sustained by Treas
ury Department.
The Secretary of the Treasury has de
cided that the Collector of Customs has
a right to refuse to grant to Chinese in
transit the jM-ivilege of passing through
any part ot the United States when he
feels that the applicants intend to make
their way clandestinely into this country.
He has decided also upon the authority
of F. A. Reeves, acting Solicitor of the
Treasury, that there can be no appeal
under the present regulations from the
judgment of the Collector. Hence the de
partment has dismissed the . appeals in
the oases of eighty Chinese laborers who
asked permission of Collector Stratton to
pass through California on the way to
ioreien countries.
Reeves makes a singular mistake and
one that does an injustice to Judge de
Haven of the United States District
Court. In his written opinion to the Sec
retary of the Treasury he insinuates that
Judge de Haven is ignorant of the geog
raphy of the republic of Mexico, and then
vqry inconsistently refers to Judge de
Haven as "the learned Judge." The fact
le that Judge de Haven In deciding in fa
vor of Collector Stratton in the cases
which were appealed to the Treasury De
partment or, the agreed case of Fok
Yung Yo said that the applicant asked
permission to pass through the United
States on his way to "Guatemala, Mcx-
Jro." This was the fact, such being the
SAVES
FLOUR
BUTTER
EGGS
ROYAL
Baking
Powder
And makes the cake lighter,
flner*flavoi*ed, more
sightly.
destination of Fok as mentioned in his
application. Whether there is a place in
Mexico known as Guatemala was not
made an issue in the case. Such was the
destination in the application, and Judge
de Haven referred to it as such, as he
was obliged to do under the pleadings.
Solicitor Reeves says:
My attention has been called to a recent de
cision of Judge de Haven, who suggests that
while this class of Chinese are not entitled
to the writ of habeas corpus, they have a
remedy by appeal to the Secretary if they are
denied landing by the Collector. The question
of the -right of appeal was not before the court,
and his remark may be taken as merely obiter
dicta and not authoritative. Besides, it is
but just to the learned Judge to assume that
the opinion to which my attention has been
called (In re Fok Yung Yo) has not been re
ported with the accuracy which should char
acterize the report of a decision of the court.
For instance. 'Judge de Haven, more than once,
inadvertently, of course, locates Guatemala In
the republic of Mexico; and quite as carelessly
he Is made to remark that the regulation of
the Treasury Department relating to Chinese
in transit, etc.. is authorized by the acts of
18SS (25 St., p. 475) and 1892 (27 St.. c. 25). The
first act prohibltsthe coming of Chinese to the
United States, and the second act prohibits the
coming of Chinese persons to this country, and
has no relation to Chinese passing in transit.
The power of the Secretary to make the regu
lation referred to Is given by article 111 of the
treaty of*lS94.
In my, opinion the right of appeal from the
decision of the Collector denying the landing
of Chinese who claim to be In transit is not
given *>y the act of 1894. Appeals in such cases
may be provided for by the Secretary under
the power given by the treaty if he should see
fit to exercise it. * . Â¦
IRONMOLDEB BOGAN AGAIN
FAILS TO GET DIVORCE
Judge Sioss Decides That His Charge
of Desertion Is Not Sus
tained.
Patrick Bogan, an ironmolder, has tried
several times to secure a divorce from
his wife, but he has not met with success.
His last attempt was made in Judge
Sloss' court yesterday, b'rt he is still the
husband of Mary Bogan. Bogan claims
he has repeatedly asked his wife to live
with, him, and wants & divorce on thi
ground of desertion oc cause she refused
to do so. . Mrs. Bogan explained her fail
ure to acquiesce in his wishes by saying
that Bogan wanted her to live in a room
"in which there was net room for a three
quarter bed." Bogan's landlady corrobo
rated her testimony.
Margaret F. Bentley -ras granted a di
vorce from Charles O. Bentley yesterday
for cruelty. Bentley is an employe of the
Southern Pacific Company. His wife tes
tified that he frequently threatened to kill
her, and vowed that if she ever brought
suit for divorce he w-_>uld defeat any ef
forts of the lawyers or courts by leaving
the State. Mrs. Bentley was awarded the
custody of her 5-year-cld son.
Charles H. Smith, treasurer of the
Southern Pacific Railroad Company, was
ordered to pay his v^'fe Josephine 5100
counsel fees and $50 coLts yesterday. The
same order directed h;m to pay her $100
per month alimony pending the appeal
made by him from the decree granted his
wife.
Divorces were granted yesterday to
Olive F. Greever Â¦ from William M.
Greever for desertion. May E. Russell
from Charles S. Russell for neglect, Re
becca Weber from A-lolph E. Weber for
neglect and Margaret Davidson from
Thomas Davidson for desertion.
Samuel Thall was granted a d'vorce
from Juliet Thall by Judge Kerrigan yes
terday. The custody of Walter, the 10
year-bld son of the couple, was awarded
to the father. Thall sued for divorce on
statutory grounds, but the charges were
not pressed. The divorce was granted for
desertion.
Mrs. J. Besusly Travis, wife of Joseph
Travie. at one time a newspaper man in
this city, was granted a divorce by Judge
Hebbard yesterday on the ground of de
aertion. They were married in Honolulu
in February, 1898.
Suits for divorce were filed yesterday
by Alfred E. Robinson .-igainst Mary Rob
inson on statutory r rounds, Bertha Hess
against "Benjamin Hess for cruelty ani
Joseph Fritz against Dennle Burke Fritz
for desertion.
Colored Club Ball To-Night.
The Colored Club of 1901 will give its
annual ball at Garibaldi Hall, 423 Broad
way, to-night. All the glad rags of San
Francisco's colored circle will be dis
played. As a special feature Bob Stewart,
champion cakewalker, will perform. Mu
sic will be rendered by the ragtime or
chestra.

MOW AVENGES
FAMILY WRONGS
Chinese Crosses Ocean
in Pursuit of Mother's
Murderers.
With Knife and Cleaver
He Lays Two Brothers
Low.
Yuen Mow occupies a cell in the City
Prison, with two charges of murderous
assault against his name. A term of im
prisonment for a period of years stares
him in the face, and yot he is supremely
fcappy, because he has wreaked venge
ance upon two men who have wronged
him and his family, ne crossed the ocean
with intent to kill them. He knows that
the men he has followed from his home
in China to this distant country have
been made to suffer for the injuries they
are alleged to have infli-.ted upon his fam
ily. For ten years he has been on the
track of two brothers and within the
past month he laid them both low with
knife and^cleaver. That he may suffer
is nothing to him. That he may suffei
the death penalty if eitner of his victims
die gives him no worry. He has securei
his revenge and is willing to suffer the
consequences.
Six weeks ago Yuen Mow murderously
attacked Yuen Toy, a servant at the res
idence of Dr. George H. Palmer, if ester
day Yuen Ling, a brother of Toy, was at
tacked, and escaped instant death by
grappling with the murderer.
Toy was cut twelve times with a knife,
and the brother was struck repeated'y
with a cleaver. Both men are in a preca
rious condition.
Yuen Ling lives at 911 Clay street and is
a tailor. Yesterday morning about 6:30
o'clock he left his house to go to work,
and just as he stepped from the door
Yuen Mow, who had been watching for
him, attacked him with the cleavir.
After being struck three times on the
head Yuen Ling grapDled with his assail
ant and succeeded in wrenching the
weapon from him and striking him a blow
on the forehead with it. Yuen Mow ran,
pursued by Yuen Ling, and took refuge
in the building on the northeast corner of
Stockton and SacrameiÂ«to streets.
Policeman John Dougherty happened to
be on a Sacramento screet car on his way
to report for duty at the Hall of Jus
tice and saw Yuen Ling standing on the
street with blood running down his ne-^k
and face. The signalman at the corner
told him that a Chinese had run into the
building, and Dougherty went after him.
He found Mow crouched in a corner of
the top floor, and he showed fight, bvt
was quickly handcuffed. Yuen Ling iden
tified him as the man who had attempted
to murder him. He was taken to the City
Prison and locked up in the "tanks' 1
pending the result of Yuen Ling's inju
ries.
Yuen Ling was sent to the Receivjrg
Hospital, where Dr. Armistead found
three incised wounds of the scalp, a frac
ture of the skull and three incised
wounds on his right hand. It is thought
that the â¢wounds wii: not prove fatal.
Yuen Mow was later '.alren to the hos
pital by Detective E<\ Gibson and the
wound on his forehead was dressed.
Yuen Mow a' leges >.hat Yuen Toy and
Yuen Ling robbed him ot his farm in Chi
na and murdered his mother. They came
to this country about ten years ago and
he had followed them, waiting for a
chance to have his "avenge.

NEW COAST DIVISION
REOPENS FOR TRAVEL
Winter Time Table of the Southern
Pacific Goes Into Effect
Shortly.
On and after December G the winter
time table of the Southern Pacific Com
pany will go into effect. The Sunset lim
ited, which leaves this city every Monday,
Wednesday and Friday, and the ast day
light express that leaves Third- and
Tpwnsend streets at 8 a. m., will travel
over the coast division. This practically
means the reopening of the coast alvi
sion. which closed down early last spring
in order that eighty-pound rails might be
laid in the place of lighter ones.
Buffet cars will be put on the coast di
vision run, and as there was complaint
that they were inadequate for the large
travel over the road dining cars will also
be attached to the trains.

Solid Republican Delegation.
The Republicans at this time are mas
ters of tne situation, and the exclusion
act will be extended through Republican
agencies. The bill will probably be
passed by a Republican House and a Re
publican Senate and be approved by a
Republican President.
According to all accounts, there is a
general desire upon the part of all the
Republican State office-holders for renom
ination. There is some talk of asking
Controller Colgan to go higher. Attorney
General Ford is also on the list of those
entitled to promotion. Lieutenant Gover
nor Neff has been asked many times to
enter the contest for the first prize on the
ticket, but he has told his friends that
Harold T. Power and E. C. Voorheis are.
miners and available.
Republican leaders fancy that some
tiling is going to happen in Alameda
County that may result in a solid dele
gation behind some favorite son of that
county. Should Victor H. Metcalf go to
the State convention heading an undivid
ed delegation of Alamedans his prospects
of success would alarm other aspirants.
The likelihood of Metcalf entering the
race has suggested to Republicans tho
name of Alden Anderson for Congress.
It will be called to mind that the Gage-
Herrin machine made a special fight
against Mr. Anderson for the Speakership
of the last Assembly, and by the assist
ance of Boss Martin Kelly succeeded in
electing Corney Pendl<non.
Gage Force Not ( Strong.
If the primary election law is not
knocked out by the Supreme Court the
Herrin-Gage forces in the next State con
vention will not be formidable. Should
the law be overthrown Burns and Herrin
would probably order the Republican
County Committee to appoint delegates
favorable to Gage. Such a rank pro
gramme would disrupt the party in San
Francisco and stir up party strife else
where, because the Republican citizens
and taxpayers of the metropolis will not
accept a Herrin-Bums programme either
in State or local affairs. Since the recent
municipal election the stock of indepen
dent, anti-boss Republican aspirants for
Governor has advanced. E. F. Preston.
Thomas Flint, E. B. Edson, Harold
Power, Frank H. Short, George C. Pardee
and others have ah equal chance with
Gage in winning the favor of local Re
publicans.
COLORED NURSE
MIXES THE DATES
March Is the First Month
of the Year, Says
Mrs. Kennedy.
Some Interesting Testimony-
Given in the Kershow
Will Contest
Mrs. Alice Kennedy, a negress of Oak
land, who cared for the late Max Ker
show, whose will is being contested, testi
fied yesterday that from April 1 to April
24 of this year, the period covering the
time when the purported will was exe
cuted, neither J. Morgan Smith nor A. J.
Meadows, tne witnesses to the will, were
in Kershow's apslttments at Tortoni's.
She said that Smith called frequently to
inquire after Kershow's health, but never
entered the rooms.
In the direct examination the colored
woman was very positive as to the dates,
but when cross-examined by Attorney
Tauszky, who represents Rhea Gettings,
to whom Kershow left most of his prop
erty, it became evident that she was la
mentably ignorant where dates were con
cerned. When asked how old she was
she said she was 1896, and followed this
remarkable statement by saying that
March was the first month of the year.
When given a chance to make another
guess she said November. The attorneys
for Miss Gettings were not slow to see
that the woman was dense, except as to
the dates in which the contestants were
interested, and plied her with questions
concerning days, months and years, prac
tically destroying her evidence. It was
also discovered that the witness had a
number of dates written on a card which
she held in her Ipn. These dates, she
claimed, were written by her husband to
enable her to answer the questions which
he informed her wculd be asked her.
Mrs. Kennedy was a better witness
when describing Kershow's habits. She
said that she was with him from 6:30
a. m. to 11 p. m. every day and that be
tween those hours he drank a bottle and
a half of whisky. She said that from the
Ist of April of this year to the 24th he
never left his room and was so weak that
he could not walk without her aid. Her
testimony in this respect corroborated
that of John Roland, the negro who re
mained with Kershow during the night.
The case was continued until 11 a. ra.
to-day.
A Book War Imminent.
Owing to the unprecedented cuts in the
prices of books by Cooper & Co., the
Market-street booksellers, the question
arises. "What will be the outcome?"
They are selling the "Crisis" and "Eben
Holden" at 85c,**the "Eternal City" and
"Helmet of Navarre" at 95c and "Quincy
Adams Sawyer" at 75c. The "Right of
Way" and "Graustark" at $1 05. Mr.
Cooper says they will continue to sell all
books at cut rates and will meet the low
est price offered in San Francisco. *
News in Army Circles.
Captain Isaac C. Jenks, Twenty-fourth
Infantry, has been assigned to duty at
the discharge and detention camps on
Angel Island. Major R. H. Wilson, Eighth^
Infantry, has been attached to the Pre
sidio casual camp. More, than 1000 re
cruits are expected to arrive in the city
before the end of the week, preparatory
to sailing for the Philippines.
Leonard Wilmore, formerly a private in
the Twenty-fifth Infantry (colored) and
now a prisoner at Alcatraz Island under
a life sentence, has been ordered trans
ferred to the United States penitentiary
at Fort Leavenworth. Kansas.

ROB COLEMAN
IN HIS SALOON
Three Footpads Strangle
Him and Take Money
and Watch.
The robbery in Joseph Coleman's sa
loon, 110 Second street, Monday evening
was one of the most daring that has ever
occurred in the city. Coleman was knock
ed down and kicked and robbed of his
gold watch and chain. The robbers also
took $42 out of the cash re'fister. Captain
Seymour has detailed Detectives Ryan
and ODea on the case, and as Coleman
was able to give a good description of the
men their arrest is expected soon.
Coleman's statement is that the three
men entered his saloon at the time men
tioned and called for three glasses of
beer. Coleman served them and one of
them put a 50-cent piece on the counter.
As Coleman turned around to get the
change from the cash register one of the
trio threw his arm around his neck and
pulled him backward against the bar.
Another grabbed his watch and chain out
of his pocket, while the third rifled the
cash register.
Coleman was unable to call for help,
as the robber's arm was strangling him.
He was thrown to the floor and kicked
on the jaw and body. The trio then ran
out of the saloon.
The police were also notified yesterday
that Saturday night, between 10 and 11
o'clock, two men entered the saloon of
A. Schoenitzer, Twenty-sixth and Bart
lett streets, and ordered two glasses of
beer. While one engaged him in conver
sation the other" succeeded in extracting
from the till a bag containing $20. He
missed the bag almost Immediately after
they had left.
The Overdue Fleet.
The American ship Edward Sewall, now
out 166 days from New York for Shanghai,
was posted as overdue yesterday. She is
laden with kerosine and 15 per cent was
paid on her by the underwriters yester
day.
The Roanoke, now out 168 days from
Norfolk, Va., took another tumble yes
terday. She was at 25 per cent, but ow
ing to the fact that she was spoken on
September 25 in latitude 54 degrees south,
longitude 79 degrees west, the rate drop
ped to 15 per cent. Soon after the Roa
noke left the coast of Virginia a vessel
was seen on fire by a passing steamer
and it was thought to be the American
ship. The underwriters paid 45 per cent
on her until it was discovered that the
Roanoke was safe and sound off the
Platte. Then a scare over her coal cargo
was gotten up and reinsurance was paid
on her until the rate again reached 35
per cent. This figure dropped to zero
when the ship was reported this side of
the Horn, but the underwriters again got
scared over the heated cargo of a vessel
that reached Honolulu and trie rate of
the Roanoke again went to 25 per cent.
Now comes the news of her having been
spoken again and the reinsurance takes
a corresponding tumble.
Re-elected Justice Court Clerk.
The Justices of the Peace met yesterday
and ie-elected Edward W. Williams chief
clerk of the Justices' Court for a term of
two years. Williams has held, the office
for ten years. He was formerly a deputy
in the County Clerk's office. During his
regime expenditures have been materially
decreased with a corresponding increase
In receipts.
Bloodhounds Trailing Bandits.
ZANESVIL-LE, Ohio. Nov. 2>s.â At New
Lexington early to-day the operator of
the Cincinnati and Muskingum Valley
Railroad was bound and gagged by
masked burglars, who dynamited the
safes of that company, the Adams Ex
press Company and the United States Ex
press Company. The burglars secured
but little money. The Sheriff is trailing
them with bloodhounds.
